Stayed here for a men's retreat and had a blast. Cabins are a bit outdated but great accomodations. Staff made sure everything was good during our weekend and did an excellent job. Shout out to our event coordinator Caleb, he made our stay worthwhile. The views are stunning from every angle, trail hikes were fun and the obstacle course, Zipline were exhilarating! Didn't want to leave this place. Great place to visit and get away from the Hussle and bustle of the city. We enjoyed everything this place has to offer.<//text>

<Review>First off, thank you to all the staff that had helped me here when i was growing up with becoming a better person and giving me someone to talk to. Just wanted to leave a review because i grew up coming here in the 2000's to early 2010s and this place changed my life, the bridge that you walk over in the middle of the camp in particular. I sat on that thing and stared down the valley almost all of the day, the freedom you feel being here is splendid. It gave me a new perspective on life but also reminded me how short it is. Met some good friends there that i sadly no longer talk to, even my first girlfriend. I hope everyone i met here is doing well in life. I gave this review 4 stars out of five only because I feel like the quality of the experience going here to camp isn't what it used to be with the changes to certain parts of the camp, but things always come to an end and life goes on. Also some solo time here is necessary to soak it all in

if you have kids and want to build a closer bond with them i highly recommend this camp and the soul purification the beautiful surroundings have to offer. Do everything in the camp. i plan to visit again sometime for the day with a close friend just to remind myself what a blessing it was to be here even though i'm no longer religious.
Come in winter when it snows too.</Review>< pics>

Clean location. Been coming here for about four months and have never had a problem with any machine. They have 5 different size washing machines (loads) and two sizes of dryers. I've never had a problem finding a machine even on busy days. The attendant doesn't do much but hang out on the table with his phone until he's needed or someone needs help. <date>1549858386748<//date><text>Not a place I would recommend for authentic Chinese food. The food is Chinese fusion. I think many people go to the restaurant because of Martin Yan's name.

The interior decor of the restaurant is unique. My favorite is the big antique bell at the bar. The seating, however, is very uncomfortable. The tables are placed too close to each other, with little room for people to walk through. The dishes look & sound creative, but the taste is really unimpressive.

For the price it charges, the customer service of this restaurant is disappointing! Most staff are courteous, but they don't know how to serve. When serving the soup, the usual Chinese etiquette is to pour the soup for all the guests at the table. But the server just put the soup and utensils on the table and left. Moreover, the Latino looking woman literally dropped the bowl of sauce in the middle of the table, and didn't even apologize for her rudeness.

Overall, the service and the food don't live up to M.Y. China's name.<//text>< gmap_id>

<text>If you are looking for a place with authentic Chinese food, this is not your place. M.Y. China is more suited for people with a heavy taste, hence why many dishes at this restaurant are spicy. Service was a bit slow but servers were quite friendly. They do have quite a verity of tea unlike most Chinese restaurants where they only serve you one kind of tea. The deserts were quite good. <user>110044408245887412132<//user><name>Tina Tsong< /name><Date>1544999948928< /Date>< rating>
3< /rating>
<Review>We waited briefly at noon on Sunday before we were seated. The dining area definitely started to get more packed while we were eating.
1) tea smoked pork belly sliders: good but there is no hint of tea flavor. The bao is soft and well steamed, but the pork belly is ordinary if not slightly bland.
2) Wild Boar Scissor Cut Noodles: the wild boar is diced into small indistinguishable pieces that it almost seemed like an afterthought in the dish. The noodles and sauce were unexpectedly commonplace in texture and flavor.
3) Dan Dan noodles: thin noodles are served cold in a peanut sauce. A lot of restaurants serve this differently, and this one is of the less notable versions.
4) Mushroom with spicy sesame sauce: the mushrooms have a great meaty texture, but one could not taste any sesame. The sauce instead bordered on the glossy sweet side.
5) eggplant and tofu clay pot: would definitely recommend for the soft tofu dredged in cornstarch and gently fried. The eggplant in the dish is cooked well
6) Yang zhou fried rice: delicious but very ordinary. Easily found and replicated by many restaurants.
7) Peking roast duck: the skin is crisp and well done. Also recommended.

M.Y. China is one of the better mall restaurants but certainly sits average among the category of americanized Cantonese food. While I will probably not return due to the conventional menu and flavors, I can definitely see it as a good alternative to the less exciting options at the mall.<//Review>< Pictures>

I cant say enough about how much I love this place. Everything is made fresh, including (and especially) the noodles. The soups are flavorful and delicious, the entrees are elegant. But one of my favorite things here is the spicy crispy tofu...I could eat that all day long! My China is on the 4th floor of the Westfield mall, so if you're having a hard time finding it, take the elevator to the 4th floor (under the dome). There is sometimes a wait, but it's usually only 10-20 mins and it's worth it!<//text>

<Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNVz020TDATP_kE_zzO9COej1D403YLmV-qlNg=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOZWEgE6hzVXrnikry5jruqqsIH2_rlUTj83FM=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPLKHsT4mbIIdiIMBwuxfRcmw6m4EOI0cGGB3U=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pictures><Gmap_id>0x808580860ca8f4fb:0x170fd44206b9ead1<//Gmap_id><user>106995104092230058741< /user><user_name>Master Maggie Li<//user_name>< rating>
4</rating>
<date>1542687282570</date>< Review>
I always forget MY China when I choose where to eat in SF. But with the horrible air quality, we decided to stay inside Westfield Mall after getting off of BART. And I'm glad we did. Sadly we missed Happy Hour (Monday-Friday 3-6PM, mostly discounted alcoholic drinks).

I highly recommend the Da Dao "Big Knife" Seafood Noodle - stir-fried noodle with generous portion of seafood (scallop, squid, shrimp), shiitake mushroom (my fav), baby oyster mushroom, pea sprouts and stringy egg. Such good work flavor! It was good to eat with other saltier dish as it was a bit bland, so I asked for some chili sauce and that definitely elevated the dish. Must-try! Eggplant tofu clay pot had pieces of soft, lightly fried tofu with chunks of eggplant. It was a soy sauce-based dish, and had some basil for flavoring; a little oily though.

Overall, great American Chinese food! But of course it was more expensive than your usual Chinese restaurant. Also they make interesting cocktaiIs. If you are a drinker, try to make it to Happy Hour.<//Review>

For de desserts. Tea infused cr√®me br√ªl√©e was okay, not very strong tea flavor. Vietnamese coffee ice cream was neither strong or creamy. It was watery, sugary sweet with not that much of coffee flavor.

Overall, good place but a bit overpriced for Chinese food.<//text>

< Text>
Mysterious vibes in the restaurant, the lighting is dark. Good for parties, friends meet ups. The  waiters were decent friendly. Noted here, the dandan noodles are served cold with sliced carrots on top which is different from originals and its not so meaty, but still worth a try. The crab dumpling was placed over a pice of veggie, server with a kind of red sweet/sour liquidish sauce, the dumplings were juicy as you would expected but fairy decent taste. Would recommend it if you wanna have dumplings once a while. Also connivence location, its located on the top floor of westfield. Right next to the elevator, easy to found. Different from the open fast restaurants on the F1, it is actually a well-decorated American Chinese restaurant.<//Text>

< Text>
I‚Äôve been there twice as it is across the street from my hotel. The positive stuff first. If you are a fan of Peking duck, they do it very well and it‚Äôs reasonably priced. One half portion is plenty for two people ($24). I‚Äôve also had the house fried rice which was good but not that special for $13 (a small portion) and any decent Chinese restaurant can do it the same and even better. Now the negative. Two extremely disappointing items were the dumpling sampler ($15 for 6) and the salt and pepper calamari. The dumplings were bland and absolutely tasteless - all 3 flavors were blech. The calamari was like eating a breaded car tire, thick breading and tough/chewy. They were equally wretched ... and I don‚Äôt get to use that word often. We were planning to order one of the Market priced lobster dishes, but at $60+ it wasn‚Äôt worth the risk when two very simple dishes were disappointments. As this seems to be a mid to higher end priced restaurant, I expected better quality for the price. I will say the wait staff is nice and somewhat attentive, but overall it was a thumbs down for us and I gave it two chances. Venture down Geary St for much better quality, variety AND value. Peking Duck and service makes it 3 stars for me.< /Text>

<Rate>4<//Rate>< Text>
Surprisingly good experience here. There can be a wait, so I recommend just reserving through OpenTable since they put priority on those with reservations (they allow same day).

If you are craving legitimate Chinese food after some shopping but are too lazy to make it to the Richmond or Chinatown, just go here!

We got the string beans, Peking duck (half), and beef noodle soup. The beef noodle soup was very good, I actually don't know where else to get this dish since sf is so lacking of authentic Taiwanese food. The Peking duck was great as well, though I wish they provided the thin pancake slices to eat with instead of the steamed buns. The string beans were pretty standard and nothing special.

The service was also really great - despite us having a seat more towards the outdoor area, our waitress Jessica was super attentive.

We are glad to have a good Peking duck option in sf, without having to trek to Berkeley.  I wouldn't mind coming back again.</Text>

< review>
M.Y. China was one of the restaurants I've walked by so many times when walking around Westfield. It never really caught my eye until I ate here. I hear the counter is the best place to sit so you can watch them prepare your food and toss the noodles around, but we usually sit outside the restaurant and watch others walk around the mall. The service is usually on-point and timely. I appreciate their tea selection. The food is also really tasty. It can be a little expensive due to it's location, but I usually find it's worth it. Don't make the mistake like I did, stop in next time you're in Westfield.</review>

One waitress cheated on the tip! My bill was $30.65, the printed tip of 20% on the bill was $10.86 which was actually more than 35%.  I am always generous on tips so I just blindly paid that number.  I just realized this cheating trick after I was back home but I didn't keep my bill.
Double check all the numbers on the bill before you pay it and keep the bill.< /Review>

<text>IF YOU HAVE FOOD ALLERGIES AVOID THIS PLACE!!!!!

TLDR: of the 2 dishes I ordered, they screwed up 4 times and would have given me a severe allergic reaction!

I went to My China on Wed evening with my CEO and several of his friends. I explained my food allergies of peppers, cayenne, chili powder and anything "spicy" to the waitress and was advised I could eat the fried chicken appetizer, rice and sweet and sour chicken.

The waitress brought the fried chicken wings and it was immediately obvious that it was covered in cayenne or chili powder with peppers on top of it. All of which I am very allergic to. The waitress apologized and promised that she would make sure it didn't happen again.

She brought out the order and promised it was fine as she had personally talked to the head chef and he was extra careful. I almost took a bite when my dining companions told me to stop because it had a ton of straight cayenne on it.

I waited for 5 minutes and went to find a manager, I spoke with another waitress who said she was on break and would come see me shortly and took the wings for a second time.

Our waitress came back apologizing again, and I reiterated my food allergies and that this was serious. She promised to make sure there was no more problems. She delivered the wings shortly after and the 3rd time, no spice, just incredibly over cooked. I assume the chef wasn't happy.

I hadn't received my main dish at this point while the others had been out for awhile. When it came, it was covered in peppers and appeared to have chili flake as well. The table tried it and reported it was spicy. At this point people were finishing up their meals and I was very embarrassed.  The group insisted on waiting until I had my dinner and ended up sitting there for 30 minutes until my food came and I finished it as fast as I could.

This whole experience was very embarrassing and is simply inexcusable.

< Review>
After hearing Martin Yan had opened a restaurant and since I had just moved to SF, it was perfect timing. I loved watching Yan Can Cook as a child and I was excited to have the opportunity to see what his restaurant had to offer.

The wild boar scissor cut noodles are a must try. They are so flavorful and have that nice "wok" flavor to them. It can be a bit salty to some palates but it goes well with the entrees. The Beijing knife cut noodles are also worth trying. They are cooked well and are a nice vegetarian option. The beef hand pulled noodles are also good. The presentation is very neat and the broth is quite tasty. But I would recommend trying the dry noodles to the noodle soups are you can taste more of the "wok" flavor and it's much easier to share. Also, the chefs sometimes put on a show as they pull the noodles right in front of your table.

My favorite entree has to be the five spice pork ribs. Don't let the word ribs deceive you into the dish being messy and hard to eat because it's quite the opposite. The meat was so tender and fell right off the bone. The pork ribs I presume is slow cooked and then fried a bit on the outside to give it that crispy golden color and taste. It's so delicious that you must try for yourself. The lamb chops are also on the top of my list. It's seasoned with cumin and chili powder and tastes so flavorful and juicy. Also, you can give the Peking duck a try. It's not the best Peking duck but it is still good and satisfies the craving.

From the small eats, the tea smoked pork belly sliders are wonderful. They are tender and goes nicely with the bun. But I have to say I've had better as the pork belly wasn't melt in your mouth.

I've made three visits here already and have loved the food and experience here each time. It's situated right under the dome at the Westfield and it's a perfect place to grab dinner and a movie. I love this place and of course I'm planning future visits.<//Review>

<Text>Yes, it's in the mall but despite that, M.Y. China serves up some pretty tasty Chinese food. They've got the standard kung pao and honey walnut shrimp that are now cornerstones in most American Chinese restaurants but things like their pork dumplings (xiao long bao) and lots of their noodles are definitely on point and delicious. Very extensive menu, nice airy interior. I'd say it's a little bit more upscale too, some of the fish and seafood entrees are pushing $40 but a good meal can definitely be had for less than that.< /Text>< Pictures>

<Rating>5</Rating><review>At this elegant establishment, Chinese cuisine is elevated to a previously unimaginable level. How? It's Martin Yan's place. 'Nuff said. Shawn C<//name>

1373430819664< /Time>
<rating>4< /rating>< Text>
I glanced in the kitchen as we were being seated and swore I saw one guy skipping rope while another was snipping a softball with scissors. The things these restaurants do these days to be different.... Turns out this is how they make the noodles. Lots of twirling in the air and snipping noodles from a ball of dough.

We ordered:
crispy springrolls - nothing special here
stir fly baby bok choy - garlic and anchovies brought it alive
honey glazed bbq pork - good but the same thing you'd get in any Chinese place
scissor-cut noodles - I liked the lumpy cut noodles
squid ink snap noodles - my favorite--delicious doughy noodles with scallops and jumbo shrimp mixed in

Plenty of food with one IPA = $67 + tip

With Chinatown a few blocks up, I'm not sure we'll be returning to the mall the next time we have a hankering for some Chinese food. But worth checking out.</Text>

<Text>Decided to check this place out after watching a Martin Yan episode on TV and heading to SF the following week. While excellent, I have to say the main course was the most disappointing. I started off with the drink of Tsingtao and a shot of a strong Chinese alcohol (like a Chinese sake or something) which I highly enjoyed. We grabbed dumplings and bao for appetizers which were incredible. For the main course I had Milk Oolong Tea and crispy noodles in XO sauce. While tasty, the sauce was overly sweet (I'd say Americanized) and I was hoping for something a little more authentic. Again, it wasn't bad, but I would order something else next time. For dessert I had the Lychee Penna Cotta which was very unique and much less sweet than the main dish. Overall a very good place.< /Text><pictures>None< /pictures><resp>None</resp>< Gmap_id>
0x808580860ca8f4fb:0x170fd44206b9ead1< /Gmap_id>
</record></dataset><record>
< Pictures>
None< /Pictures>
< Review>
M.Y. China is a hidden gem in the Westfield mall in Downtown San Francisco. Its one of the restaurants "Under the Dome". Though it is located in a mall, this place has great ambiance (perfect for date night) and the food here is A-M-A-Z-I-N-G! We ordered the crispy tofu, scissor cut noodles with tofu and Kung Pao Tofu! Yes, it is a lot of tofu but we became a fan with the first bit we took of crispy tofu. This was the best tofu my wife and I have had every period. It melts in your mouth yet doesn't break that easily. The crispy tofu was perfectly crisp and nicely spiced. We will be coming here again to try out other dishes, specially the long noodles which are famous here.

Tip: if you like lychee, try the lychee panna cota dessert here, you will regret not trying it!< /Review>
